    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<span id="freeTextContainer17010381579361591825"><b>A masterful tale of ambition, jealousy, desire, and superpowers.</b><br/><br/>Victor and Eli started out as college roommates—brilliant, arrogant, lonely boys who recognized the same sharpness and ambition in each other. In their senior year, a shared research interest in adrenaline, near-death experiences, and seemingly supernatural events reveals an intriguing possibility: that under </span>
  <span id="freeText17010381579361591825" style="display:none"><b>A masterful tale of ambition, jealousy, desire, and superpowers.</b><br /><br />Victor and Eli started out as college roommates—brilliant, arrogant, lonely boys who recognized the same sharpness and ambition in each other. In their senior year, a shared research interest in adrenaline, near-death experiences, and seemingly supernatural events reveals an intriguing possibility: that under the right conditions, someone could develop extraordinary abilities. But when their thesis moves from the academic to the experimental, things go horribly wrong.<br /><br />Ten years later, Victor breaks out of prison, determined to catch up to his old friend (now foe), aided by a young girl whose reserved nature obscures a stunning ability. Meanwhile, Eli is on a mission to eradicate every other super-powered person that he can find—aside from his sidekick, an enigmatic woman with an unbreakable will. Armed with terrible power on both sides, driven by the memory of betrayal and loss, the archnemeses have set a course for revenge—but who will be left alive at the end?<br /><br />In <i>Vicious</i>, V. E. Schwab brings to life a gritty comic-book-style world in vivid prose: a world where gaining superpowers doesn't automatically lead to heroism, and a time when allegiances are called into question.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17010381579361591825" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<a href="/questions/223945-can-ya-fans-of-victoria-schwab-read-and">Can YA fans of Victoria Schwab read and enjoy this book too? Why is it listed as both adult and young adult?</a>
</div>

<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_223945'><a id="like_count_community_question_223945" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/223945?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">1 like</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F40874032-vicious">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/15132897-tamara-stovall"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1541245085i/15132897._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/15132897-tamara-stovall">Tamara Stovall</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think YA fans would enjoy the story but there is adult content that would result in an R rating if this were a movie. Cursing (including the F-word)<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think YA fans would enjoy the story but there is adult content that would result in an R rating if this were a movie. Cursing (including the F-word) and extreme violence (including violence with firearms and torture).<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/662870422" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/662870422?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765335340" href="/book/show/13638125-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer662870422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9047780218122474645"><b>"Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human."</b><br/><br/>I actually received an 100-page preview of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious' title='Vicious by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vicious</a> a few months prior to reading the full version and picked it up with absolutely zero expectations. Then, suddenly, I was catapulted into a world that did more than keep the promises of the blurb - <i>A masterful, twisted tale of ambition, jealousy, betrayal, and superpowers, set in a near-future world</i> - but also introduced me to a memorable cast of characters,</span>
  <span id="freeText9047780218122474645" style="display:none"><b>"Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human."</b><br /><br />I actually received an 100-page preview of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious" title="Vicious by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> a few months prior to reading the full version and picked it up with absolutely zero expectations. Then, suddenly, I was catapulted into a world that did more than keep the promises of the blurb - <i>A masterful, twisted tale of ambition, jealousy, betrayal, and superpowers, set in a near-future world</i> - but also introduced me to a memorable cast of characters, an exciting plot, and some of the most addictive writing I've ever read.<br /><br />Schwab's other books never appealed to me but I suddenly find myself wanting to see if all her writing is like this. Some books just have that spark. It's a compulsive readability in the writing style; it demands to be read; it demands that you keep turning pages like a crazy person. You can't really explain or define it, you can only point to examples of where it exists. And it exists here. Everything about this book draws you in: the characters, the plot, the way the book moves fluidly from past to present... everything. I can't tell you how much <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious" title="Vicious by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> surprised me, and I can't find words to explain just how exciting, gripping and beautifully twisted it is. But I shall try.<br /><br />Vicious falls into the adult/new adult category as opposed to young adult. To break it down simply, this is a story about superheroes and supervillains and how it isn't always so easy to tell which is which. Victor questions at one point:<br /><br /><b>"The paper called Eli a hero.<br />The word made Victor laugh. Not just because it was absurd, but because it posed a question. If Eli really was a hero, and Victor meant to stop him, did that make him a villain?"</b><br /><br /> It's all about the ambitions, the betrayals and the jealousies of people who are far too clever for their own good. People who work together to obtain power but whose friendship is torn apart by said power. The characters - including the protagonist - all have dark sides hiding beneath their calm, collected exteriors. Perhaps this will put some readers off, but I was absolutely fascinated by the exploration of the fine line between the good guys and the bad guys.<br /><br />The story is split between the present and ten years ago. The present tells of Victor, an escaped convict, who is determined to find his old friend-turned-enemy and deal out the revenge that is burning inside him. Flash back to ten years ago and Victor is a bright, young university student who is practically inseparable from his best friend - Eli. When Eli proposes a plan to discover whether EOs (Extra-Ordinaries) exist, he and Victor become partners in a scheme that will take them to hell and back and maybe, just maybe, grant them supernatural abilities. I adored the complex friendship between the two men that hovered somewhere between admiration and bitter jealousy and how this developed as they grew and became more obsessed with power and their own view of right and wrong.<br /><br />I loved Vicious, I really did. I'd easily consider it one of my favourite novels of 2013 and probably the one that surprised me most. It's just a wild and addictive story with no throwaway characters. Everyone in the book has their own problems to face, especially when it comes to some of the moral struggles that go with having godlike powers. I can't wait for more people to read it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9047780218122474645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer189903479345678528">You know that feeling of nostalgia you get when you're reading one of your favorite books? <br/><br/>That's how I felt the whole time I was reading this. <br/><br/>It was like I already knew this world and these characters. And that's not to say that they were bland or stereotypical (because they were extremely complex and compelling), but it was as if they were already somehow part of my life. <br/><br/>I don't even have the words to describe how much I loved this. It was perfect, absolutely perfect. </span>

          </span>

    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2059043244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1808974261846316214"><i>”Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. Someone else could be labelled a villain for trying to stop them. Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.”</i><br/><br/>(Just in case you actually want to read my full review. *lol* You can read it <a href='thesassylibraryfox.wordpress.com/2019/08/28/review-vicious-v-e-schwab/' rel='nofollow noopener'>here!</a>)<br/><br/>This is easily one of the best books I’ve read in 2019 and that’s quite something, because I already read so many other awesome books this year. To give <b>“Vicious”</b> 5 stars was a no-brain</span>
  <span id="freeText1808974261846316214" style="display:none"><i>”Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. Someone else could be labelled a villain for trying to stop them. Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.”</i><br /><br />(Just in case you actually want to read my full review. *lol* You can read it <a href="thesassylibraryfox.wordpress.com/2019/08/28/review-vicious-v-e-schwab/" rel="nofollow noopener">here!</a>)<br /><br />This is easily one of the best books I’ve read in 2019 and that’s quite something, because I already read so many other awesome books this year. To give <b>“Vicious”</b> 5 stars was a no-brainer though and I’m very glad that my reading buddy saw it the same way. As it seems we were both hooked right from the beginning and the longer we read, the more we immersed ourselves in the story.<br /><br />I thought long and hard about the many reasons I liked this so much and I think it’s mostly due to the way it was written. V.E. Schwab made her story some sort of puzzle and the longer you read, the more is revealed and every piece eventually falls into place. It wasn’t until I started to write down a few of the quotes that I finally realized why I could relate to her writing style so much. XD It felt like reading one of my forum role-play games. *lol*<br /><br />Let me explain a little bit more: There are people that will write short posts that cover the basics and then there are people that will write an entire character with its background story and play it out in 900 – 1.000 word posts that stretch over the course of years, sometimes even decades. Yes, you already guessed right, I’m the latter one. ;-P And so it’s no surprise I was intrigued by V.E. Schwab’s handiwork. <br /><br />There’s a certain depth to her characters you never actually see on the pages, but it’s all there, in their actions, the way they behave. In the way they talk and interact with each other. There’s an entire background story and we get it piece by piece, little by little, but never all of it and to say I was captivated by this would be the understatement of the century. XD I lived and breathed for it, I tasted blood and I crave for more!!! &lt;3<br /><br />Next time I’m at the library I’m going to pre-order “Vengeful” and if it’s only half as good as “Vicious” I shall be more than just fine! ;-) This said, I’ll go right into my character’s section because damn, there’s a lot to discuss! XD<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Welcome to my spoilery spoiler section! Take a seat, make yourself comfortable and enjoy the show! Be warned though, I’m at least as fierce as Victor when it comes to book characters and just like him I won’t sugar-coat things and spoil you not only thoroughly but also relentlessly! ;-P</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Eli Cardale (Ever):</b><br /><br /><i>”Well, when you wonder something,” said Eli, “doesn’t that mean part of you wants to believe in it? I think we want to prove things, in life, more than we want to disprove them. We want to believe.”</i><br /><br />I didn’t like Eli which actually made him the perfect villain. *lol* The funny thing is that I’m pretty certain he’s more human and compassionate than Victor, yet this also seems to be the main reason why he’s worse than him. Am I already confusing you? XD Okay, let me put it this way, whilst Victor’s analytical mind controls his actions the same can’t be said about Eli. When the shit hits the fan Eli is following his gut feeling and because he believes he’s doing the right thing he goes through with it and never second guesses his decisions. I’d even go as far as to say that Eli is some sort of religious fanatic and that he sanctions his actions by his belief. And what is more human and more powerful than people’s beliefs? There are centuries of history that prove how many bad things have been done in the name of religion and Eli’s character is some kind of embodiment of it. He lives by his principles and this doesn’t only make him a very dangerous man, it also makes him very human. Eli is on a mission and everyone who interferes with it will be the next victim on his Ever-growing list. ;-) (see what I did there?! *lol*)<br /><br /><i>”On the surface, Eli seemed perfectly normal, but now and then Victor would catch a crack, a sideways glance, a moment when his roommate’s face and his words, his look and his meaning, would not line up. Those fleeting slices fascinated Victor. It was like watching two people, one hiding in the other’s skin. And their skin was always too dry, on the verge of cracking and showing the color of the thing beneath.”</i><br /><br /><i>”A hero. Wasn’t he? Heroes saved the world from villains, from evil. Heroes sacrificed themselves to do it. Was he not bloodying his hands and his soul to set the world right? Did he not sacrifice himself every time he stripped away an EO’s stolen life?”</i><br /><br /><i>”I died begging for the strength to survive, and it was granted. But it’s a trade, Professor, with God or the devil, and I’ve paid for my gift with the lives of my friends. Every EO has sold a part of themselves they can never have back. Don’t you see?” He knelt beside Lyne, whose fingers twitched. “I can’t let anyone else sin so heinously against nature.”</i><br /><br /><b>Victor Vale:</b><br /><br /><i>”She watched him as he worked, his touch impossibly light, as if he was afraid of breaking her. Everything about him was light – his skin, his hair, his eyes, his hands as they danced through the air above her skin, touching her only when absolutely necessary.”</i><br /><br />I absolutely ADORED AND LOVED Victor Vale!!! &lt;333 What an intriguing and morally grey character! I just loved the way he thought! His analytical and cunning mind was everything I ever craved for and even more and I just couldn’t get enough of his character. I loved that he was so unapologetic and that he knew exactly who he was. Yes, he tried to blend in with the others, but he never claimed to be something that he wasn’t. If you ask me I’d say Victor is a psychopath, at least if you consider all the typical signs of it. Then again Eli certainly was one too. He might have been more empathic than Victor but whilst Vic knew what was expected of him, Eli ultimately seemed more inclined to ignore human morals than to follow them. I loved how Victor questioned his actions, how he paused to think if what he did was right or wrong, how he weighted both sides against each other and then eventually decided to do what his logic told him. He was vicious and brutal, but he could also be gentle and caring and boy, did I live for that moral ambiguity. *lol* <br /><br /><i>”The paper called Eli a hero.<br />The word made Victor laugh. Not just because it was absurd, but because it posed a question. If Eli really was a hero, and Victor meant to stop him, did that make him a villain?<br />He took a sip of his drink, tipped his head back against the couch, and decided he could live with that.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Victor watched his friend, mesmerized by the transformation. He himself could mimic most emotions and pass them off as his, but mimicking only went so far, and he knew he could never match this … fervor.”</i><br /><br /><i>”You can’t kill me, Victor,” said Eli. “You know that.”<br />Victor’s smile widened as he buried his knife between Eli’s ribs. <br />“I know,” he said loudly. He had to speak up over the screams. “But you’ll have to indulge me. I’ve waited so long to try.”</i><br /><br /><b>Sydney:</b><br /><br /><i>”That’s what Sydney was giving these people. A second chance. <br />Her fingers hovered over the dead man’s chest for a moment as she wondered if he deserved a second chance, then chided herself. Who was she to judge or decide or grant or deny? Simply because she could, did that mean she should?”</i><br /><br />Poor little Sydney! I felt so sorry for her! She didn’t choose to have a power like that but she was hunted for it nevertheless. I found it interesting that she was so young but already asked herself the right questions. In some way that made her a good counterweight to Victor and Eli. I mean there is this powerful girl and she has no idea what she can do with her abilities or what she’s capable of. She was a very strong character though and I loved her for her defiance. &lt;3 It takes guts to live with a man like Victor and she might have questioned his actions but she was never afraid of him. XD<br /><br /><b>Serena:</b><br /><br /><i>”She looked at Victor’s profile one last time, and tried to picture the man who had once been Eli’s friend, who had brought him back, made him what he was, saved her sister … and for a moment, as she finished dialing Eli’s number, she almost wished he stood a fighting chance.”</i><br /><br />Now Serena was a character that caused me to think long and hard as well. On the one hand I liked her for standing up to Eli by charming him to do her will, and on the other hand I disliked her for helping him to find and eliminate his targets. If she was so good at compelling people why didn’t she try to stop Eli for good? She played him, yet at the same time she did what he wanted her to do. Why? Did she really think that this was the only way to save her own skin? Did she truly believe that EO’s are dangerous and that they deserve to die? Her character posed so many questions and to my chagrin none of them were answered. &gt;_&lt; She definitely had one of the best scenes in this book though. The moment Victor killed her and quoted Ulysses was priceless!! &lt;3 <br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Victor &amp; Eli:</u><br /><br /><i>”You asked me if I ever wanted to believe in something. I do. I want to believe in this. I want to believe that there’s more.” Victor sloshed a touch of whiskey over the edge of his glass. “That we could be more. Hell, we could be heroes.”<br />“We could be dead,” said Eli.<br />“That’s a risk everyone takes by living.”</i><br /><br />Ohh those two gave me a lot to wonder about. I’m convinced Victor was in love with Eli and that this was the reason why he wanted his revenge so badly. I mean he was betrayed by the person he loved and to make it even worse Eli didn’t even bother to hear him out. He didn’t give him the benefit of the doubt, no, he ratted him out to the police the moment he knew his girlfriend had died. It was like Eli always expected Victor to go off the rails and only waited for an opportunity to turn on him. Funnily enough it turned out that Eli was the one that actually went off the rails in the end. After all Eli’s girlfriend was the only person Victor killed and this was by accident and not intentional. The same certainly couldn’t be said for Eli though. He killed his victims on purpose and went after them with a vengeance. Sure, once Victor got out of prison his death tally went up as well, he never killed without a purpose or reason though. Which is the main difference between those two. Victor always considered the pros and cons while Eli acted as judge and executioner and didn’t even give his victims a chance to defend themselves, let alone to speak. Now that Eli is in prison I can’t help but wonder what’s going to happen next. I guess I’ll find out once I get my hands on a copy of “Vengeful”. ;-P<br /><br /><i>”He and Eli were bonded, by blood and death and science. They were alike, more so now than ever. And he had missed Eli. He wanted to see him. And he wanted to see him suffer. He wanted to see the look in Eli’s eyes when he lit them up with pain. He wanted his attention. Eli was like a thorn beneath Victor’s skin, and it hurt. He could turn off every nerve in his body, but Victor couldn’t do a damned thing about the twinge he felt when he thought of Cardale.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I don’t want to see Serena,” said Sydney.<br />“I know,” said Victor. “But I want to see Eli.”<br />“Why?” she asked. “You can’t kill him.”<br />“That may be.” His fingers curled around the shovel. “But half the fun is trying.”</i><br /><br /><u>Sydney &amp; Victor:</u><br /><br /><i>”I’m cold,” she said.<br />“I’m Victor,” he said, and she offered him a small, exhausted flicker of a smile.</i><br /><br />Their relationship was so precious! &lt;3 Victor became some sort of father figure for Sydney and even though she knew that he had a bad moral compass she still trusted him and felt safe with Victor. I loved that he was always so honest with her and didn’t even try to sugar-coat things. He gave her room to come to her own conclusions and he provided a safe environment to live in. In some way that made him an amazing father even though he certainly wasn’t the best choice to raise a kid like her. *lol* Still, those two worked because Sydney acted as some sort of conscience for him and that ultimately made him a better person. XD I wonder if their relationship is going to change after she brought him back from the dead and if yes in which direction it’s going to head. Oh and I just realized that Vic joined Eli in not being able to age. ;-)<br /><br /><i>”Sydney, look at me.” He rested his hands on the car roof and leaned in. “No one is going to hurt you. Do you know why?” She shook her head, and Victor smiled. “Because I’ll hurt them first.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Serena hadn’t told Sydney to go home. She hadn’t told her to run away. She’d told her to go somewhere safe. And over the course of the last week, safe had ceased to be a place for Sydney, and had become a person. <br />Specifically, safe had become Victor.”</i><br /><br /><u>Serena &amp; Eli:</u><br /><br /><i>”She pulled away enough to hold him with her cold blue eyes. He could see the devil in them, silver-tongued and cunning, and Eli thought, not for the first time, that he should have killed her when he had the chance.”</i><br /><br />Serena and Eli had one of the most abusive relationships I ever witnessed. They both abused each other in equal measure and this was weirdly fascinating. Their dynamic was crazy and they both didn’t hesitate to use their powers in order to get what they wanted. I think in some way they even loved each other, yet they both couldn’t change the way they were. Eli craved to kill Serena but was fascinated by her and Serena wanted to stay alive but couldn’t seem to be able to turn away from Eli. What a stalemate. XD Wicked faerie tongues (like mine) would say Victor relieved them from the trouble of killing each other and they might be right. *lol*<br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />I loved this and I could kick myself for not reading it sooner! <b>“Vicious”</b> was the amazing start of a compelling story and I can’t wait to read its sequel <b>“Vengeful”</b>. Morally grey characters, a captivating storyline and the omnipresent question of what is right and what is wrong made this a truly thrilling journey! I don’t know about you, but I want more! ;-)<br /><br />Last but not least I want to thank <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/99779228-craig" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Babygreys</a> for another great buddy read! It’s always a pleasure to read books with you and I’m glad our reading habits and preferences are so similar. *lol* We seem to be on a roll, let’s keep those books coming! ;-P</span>
  <a data-text-id="1808974261846316214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4742488610963289656">*EDIT*<br/>I re-read Vicious for another book club 4 years on and I still really enjoyed it! This time it was closer to a 4 star read - I wanted a little more development with some of the charcters.<br/><br/>First-read rating: 5<br/>Wow. <br/>I absolutely loved Vicious, it kept me hooked right from the get-go and as things got more and more intense, I could not put it down!<br/>I plan on filming a full review soon alongside the #LittleBookClub liveshow, so I will be back with more detailed thoughts!<br/>Verdict: READ IT YO :)</span>

<div id="review_729148703" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/729148703" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/729148703?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765335340" href="/book/show/13638125-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer729148703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1974434326090964464"><b>A Tale of Two Sociopaths.</b><br/><i>One is just ever so slightly more lovable than the other...</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422541790ra/13512790.gif' width='300' height='150' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was right up my alley with all the Create-A-Superhero stuff!<br/>The reality, of course, is that neither of these guys are <i>heroes</i>. <br/>Victor and Eli were college roommates who experimented with a theory that Eli had about how Extra Ordinary people were created. Turns out he was right. <br/><i>
  <b>Ta-da!</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422541401ra/13512746.gif' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Due to some unfortunate factors, Victor's <i>transformation</i> doesn't go quite as smoothly as Eli's. And because of that little </span>
  <span id="freeText1974434326090964464" style="display:none"><b>A Tale of Two Sociopaths.</b><br><i>One is just ever so slightly more lovable than the other...</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422541790ra/13512790.gif" width="300" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was right up my alley with all the Create-A-Superhero stuff!<br>The reality, of course, is that neither of these guys are <i>heroes</i>. <br>Victor and Eli were college roommates who experimented with a theory that Eli had about how Extra Ordinary people were created. Turns out he was right. <br><i>
  <b>Ta-da!</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422541401ra/13512746.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Due to some unfortunate factors, Victor's <i>transformation</i> doesn't go quite as smoothly as Eli's. And because of that little <i>snafu</i>, Victor ends up spending the better part of a decade in prison. <br><b>
  <i>Where he plots his <s>revahnge</s> revenge!</i>
</b><br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422542984ra/13512986.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The whole story unfolds in flashbacks, and I think the less I say about that, the more you'll enjoy reading about how it all went down in the past.<br>I do think you should know that neither of them are sympathetic characters, but you do end up rooting for Victor to <i>win</i>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422541219ra/13512731.gif" width="350" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I gotta say, I thought the ending was a little underwhelming, but that may only be because I thought the rest of the book was <i>so good</i> that it didn't quite meet my expectations. <br>Still, I ended up tearing through this thing in a few days and thought it was (overall) a pretty fantastic story.<br><b>Definitely Recommended!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422543479ra/13513067.gif" width="300" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>*Edit:<br><i>This is one of my oldest son's favorite books. He informed me the other day that he found this review while searching Goodreads at school (OMG! What the hell are they thinking giving these kids access to book sites!?), and he proceeded to tell me that I was wrong. <br>As children do...<br>Apparently, the ending was not at all underwhelming. It whelmed just fine, thank you very much.<br>So there.</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1974434326090964464" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1808131757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1808131757" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1808131757?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765335340" href="/book/show/13638125-vicious">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Katerina by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/49594567-johnnyboy">JohnnyBoy</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1808131757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4630063397967204026"><b>Vicious (adj.):</b><br/>1) Having the nature or quality of vice or immorality.<br/>2) Dangerously aggressive, marked by violence or ferocity.<br/>3) <b>Victor Vale.</b><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Victor was out. Victor was free.<br/>And Victor was coming for Eli - just as he'd promised he would.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Eli and Victor used to be best friends. Smarter than the rest of the students of Lockland University, they tried to play God. Fascinated by the rumors about EOs, ExtraOrdinary people with supernatural abilities, they studied them at first, but late</span>
  <span id="freeText4630063397967204026" style="display:none"><b>Vicious (adj.):</b><br>1) Having the nature or quality of vice or immorality.<br>2) Dangerously aggressive, marked by violence or ferocity.<br>3) <b>Victor Vale.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Victor was out. Victor was free.<br>And Victor was coming for Eli - just as he'd promised he would.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Eli and Victor used to be best friends. Smarter than the rest of the students of Lockland University, they tried to play God. Fascinated by the rumors about EOs, ExtraOrdinary people with supernatural abilities, they studied them at first, but later, they decided to create them. But the sacrifices they hade to make in order to achieve this transformation took something away. Their fear. Their conscience. Victor went to jail because of Eli, but he escaped with one goal in mind. Destroy his nemesis. His best friend. While Eli dedicated his life to the eradication of EOs, since he considered them as something unholy, Victor dedicated his life to revenge. The ultimate fight is inevitable. The question is, who will survive?<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“But it's a trade, Professor, with God or the devil...” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Wow.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457233308ra/18336703.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> was a <b>delicious surprise</b>, the perfect way to start 2017. While I did not enjoy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a> as much as I expected, after some coaxing and a mix of curiosity and hope, I decided to give <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7168230.V_E__Schwab" title="V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">V.E. Schwab</a> another try, and I am so glad I did. I dived into a <b>gripping and wicked tale of revenge and superpowers</b>, with characters who were, well, <b>psychopaths</b> but extremely <b>fascinating</b>, and while the concept reminded me of <b>X-Men</b> and the rivalry between Magneto and Professor X, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7168230.V_E__Schwab" title="V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">V.E. Schwab</a> followed a different path. Eli wanted the extermination of his kind. He fancied himself as a hero, a crusader blessed by God to rid the world of these unnatural beings and protect the innocents who were endangered by this lack of balance. Victor, on the other hand, could not care less. He was fixated on his desire to make Eli pay, using his cunning and devious mind, and a young girl with an ability that rattled Eli. A girl also hunted and betrayed.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“There are no good men in this game.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a>, what bothered me was the lack of connection with the characters. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a>, <b>I relished this detachment.</b> Victor and Eli were <b>morally grey</b> (borderline black), so I could not actually empathize with them. They were victims of their ambitions and the circumstances, villainous masterminds who, instead of being repulsed, they embraced all the ugly things that had to be done. Even Sydney, the young EO girl, lost her innocence. And so, I savored every time they outmaneuvered each other, every plan and move that led to the final confrontation, mesmerized by the twists and turns, the action, the suspense. And I have to admit that Victor intrigued me in an I-know-you-are-a-bad-person-but-still-I-root-for-you way.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483297935ra/21599045.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13638125.Vicious__Villains___1_" title="Vicious (Villains, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vicious</a> is <b>an ingenious story</b> I absolutely recommend to all those readers who crave <b>paranormal</b> with a dash of <b>twisted</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4630063397967204026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2681740494" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2681740494" />
    <a title=" Teodora " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"><img alt=" Teodora " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582144281p2/69603149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2681740494?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781783290215" href="/book/show/42289412-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=on-app">on-app</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=adult-new-adult">adult-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69603149-teodora?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2681740494" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9964783947147242050">5/5 ⭐<br/><u>
  <b>Buckle up, there's a rant ahead.</b>
</u><br/><br/>You know a book is going to obsess the hell out of me when I fall in love with the main character from the first chapters and the main character happens to be a villain.<br/><i>*Whoopsie*</i><br/>It’s true.<br/><br/>I was barely three chapters in, the time was 1 in the morning and I already decided that I am definitely going to love this. And big surprise, <i>I did.</i><br/><br/>You know why? Lemme tell you.<br/>Because there is something completely mesmerising about the way V.E. Schwab writes. If you a</span>
  <span id="freeText9964783947147242050" style="display:none">5/5 ⭐<br><u>
  <b>Buckle up, there's a rant ahead.</b>
</u><br><br>You know a book is going to obsess the hell out of me when I fall in love with the main character from the first chapters and the main character happens to be a villain.<br><i>*Whoopsie*</i><br>It’s true.<br><br>I was barely three chapters in, the time was 1 in the morning and I already decided that I am definitely going to love this. And big surprise, <i>I did.</i><br><br>You know why? Lemme tell you.<br>Because there is something completely mesmerising about the way V.E. Schwab writes. If you are not completely hooked from the first pages then there must have happened something (wrong) with either you or V.E. (maybe something <i>ExtraOrdinary</i>, who knows!).<br><br>There is madness in this woman’s mind and I think I might go mad out of my own mind if I were to have a glimpse on what’s going on in V.E. Schwab Circus of Freaks – her brain edition.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592382382ra/29661519.gif" width="275" height="190" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>The <b>atmosphere</b> is heavy, you can feel it from the beginning and it just persists through the whole book. It is macabre and dark and evil and a bit psycho but that’s the whole point of it.<br><br>I love the way the <b>world</b> is built to look like our real world, but it is completely twisted and reinvented so that we live in something we think we know but we actually don’t because it is completely new and strange – a possible near-future, if you will. There is some sort of fake-security about this world.<br><br>The <b>storyline</b> tends to jump from one time to another – in present, two days earlier, one week earlier, ten years earlier etc. etc. The chapters and the time switches alternates and it feels like they are having a conversation that you must pay attention to in order to discover all the little puzzle pieces and put them together to form the whole picture.<br>It also breaks the writing style routine a bit, makes it funkier.<br><br>The funny thing about this book is that there are no good guys, basically.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Some could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. Someone else could be labelled a villain for trying to stop them.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>It is all about perspective. Good and bad are always subjective aspects of one’s life and they always need a determinative factor to keep them going around in circles. Good is never good enough for some, or too good for others. Good can be twisted and turned into bad. Good could be worse than bad. Bad might not be as bad as it seems. Bad could be terrible.<br><br>At some point, those two notions could be interchangeable. It’s all about semantics, really. And that little fact just adds to the whole story some spice.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592382618ra/29661529.gif" width="315" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>The way the characters are being shaped in this book is fabulous.<br>The characters themselves are some sort of stereotypes, but there is something about them that makes them feel different, unique. And that something might be the skilful character building.<br><br>I don’t know how my obsession with Victor Vale could get any deeper, but I honestly think it’ll find a way.<br><br><b>I love Victor Vale, my perfect beautiful villain.</b><br><br>Victor is a morally degraded, morally grey, morally detached evil genius, constructed with such a character depth that I honestly do not meet very often. Inside of him, there is a battle between the cruelty and coldness of a predator and the ache to do the right thing. Not good, but right.<br><br>He is complex and fascinating. On the inside, Victor has doubts, struggles, tries his best to meet the ultimate outcome of his plans. Everything that comes out of his erosive thoughts though seems calculated, perfect, mischievous, sexy. Yes, you read correctly. <i>Sexy.</i><br><br>I find Victor Vale extremely hot when he is playing predator. It’s absolutely mesmerising and I am not going to apologise for it. That’s a twisted kind of magnetism that no one could resist.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1592382768ra/29661549.gif" width="260" height="155" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>On the other hand, Eli Ever repels me. He is supposed to be a hero. Well, I think he is not. And I sort of disliked him from the beginning. <br>He is a hypocrite and even though I find him bad, he is not good at being bad. He is just bad.<br><br>The problem is that Eli wasn’t made to be evil and becoming the way he is now ruined him for good. Eli was made to be the all-American charming-smile guy, but when he pushes his luck further than he can control it, then the frustration is greater than anticipated. An inner struggle like Eli’s could break down one’s morals forever, turning them into actual monsters.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>With great power comes great responsibility and not everyone can handle either of those. The outcome could be destroying. And everyone is vicious when it comes to power.<br><br>Betrayal? Revenge? Hatred?<br>Yes. All of those come in the same package with viciousness. Power makes us hungry and degrades us. It dehumanises.<br><br>The proof? Two friends like Victor and Eli wanted to kill each other because of the incredible power they both possess. There’s no friendship when it comes to power. Only hunger.<br><br>On a more positive note, this book comes with a big friendly chocolate milk lover giant with beefy arms, shaved head and tattoos, a cute little girl with a morbid power and a giant black doggo named Dol (more like <i>Doll</i>, if you ask me). Also, in an abnormal way, I find Serena kind of a baddie.<br><br>To hell with it, this is so complex and good and bad and smart and everything you need in life.<br>New favourite book with new favourite characters for my lists? You bet your cute bums. V.E. Schwab did it again.<br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1592382965i/29661558.png" width="260" height="190" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/d1fb8ce1-34c0-46ce-9919-500f53587cd9_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9964783947147242050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1902165598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902165598" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1902165598?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250160263" href="/book/show/36342017-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=plot-twists">plot-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=genre-experiments">genre-experiments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=trope-subversion">trope-subversion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=identity">identity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=author-love">author-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1902165598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10237067756321568996"><i>Vicious</i> is the story of a villain and a hero. Or, that's what it disguises itself as. It's really the story of five different morally grey characters, all out for themselves, battling it out. This is a book that <b>explores the hero / villain dichotomy and promptly shatters it to pieces.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. Someone could be labeled a villain for trying to stop that person. Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to pl</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10237067756321568996" style="display:none"><i>Vicious</i> is the story of a villain and a hero. Or, that's what it disguises itself as. It's really the story of five different morally grey characters, all out for themselves, battling it out. This is a book that <b>explores the hero / villain dichotomy and promptly shatters it to pieces.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. Someone could be labeled a villain for trying to stop that person. Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.</i>
</blockquote><br />I love books that <b>subvert and explore tropes</b>.<br /><br />Vicious sets itself apart from Schwab's other adult releases with a far faster pace. My main complaint about Darker Shade of Magic was the lack of character-driven plot; events happened to the characters rather than because of them. That's not true here. <b>Every single plot twist is due to an action by a main character.</b><br /><br />In terms of characters, this book absolutely rocks. Schwab's characters have such clear motivation for everything they do. Not a single character here is particularly good; everyone is a solid chaotic neutral except for Eli, who's one of the best lawful evil antagonists I've ever read. <br /><br /><b>Interlude: Me Ranting About How Much I Love These Characters</b><br /><i>“they're evil you shouldn't love them” we all have problematic faves</i><br /><br />Victor is the technical villain, but he's far easier to root for and empathize with. Eli is a believable, well-developed character, but his cruel fanaticism isn't a well-sold brand. Maybe Eli has a moral code and Victor doesn't, but Eli is lying to himself about his motives. Victor is evil, but he's absolutely aware of his place in the narrative, which made him easy to root for. <br /><br />Schwab's development of these characters makes the book's main conflict even more high-stakes. She also shows off her talent for relationship building here; the conflict between Victor and Eli is so dynamic and interesting. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>The difference between Victor and Eli, he suspected, wasn't their opinion on EOs. It was their reaction to them. Eli seemed intent to slaughter them, but Victor didn't see why a useful skill should be destroyed, just because of its origin.</i>
</blockquote><br />I'm always ready to read about friends-to-enemies relationships, and Victor and Eli's is especially cool. Even more so because they have genuinely touching moments. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Tell you what,” said Victor. “You remember me, and I'll remember you, and that way we won't be forgotten.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />But they're not the only interesting, 3-D characters here. Serena and Sydney are two incredibly compelling characters, and their sisterly conflict makes them ever more interesting. Sydney is a 13-year-old girl who can raise the dead. Serena can make everyone around her follow her suggestions. Despite being on “evil” sides, these two girls are so believable and their motivations so clear that <b>it's hard not to root for their respective sides.</b> I hated Eli, yet I rooted for Serena, despite her being on his side. The other side characters are equally as developed. I especially loved Mitch; he's a criminal down on his luck. <br /><br />Possibly my favorite thing was the odd familial dynamic between Mitch, Victor, Sydney, and Dol the dog. The dynamic between Victor and Sydney is totally awesome. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>Safe had ceased to be a place for Sydney. It had become a person. <br />Specifically, safe had become Victor.</i>
</blockquote><br />(Tell me you didn't cry reading that. You're LYING.)<br />Mitch and Sydney and Mitch and Victor's relationships both stand out as well. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I don't need a bodyguard,” said Victor. <br />“I noticed that,” said Mitch.<br />Victor let out a cough of a laugh. “Yes, well. I don't want everyone else to notice too.”<br />“So what do you want?” he asked.<br />Victor's lips curled into that same dangerous smile. “A friend.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I don't know if I can pick a favorite character here! They're all so interesting and memorable. <br /><br />Definitely recommended for any fans of morally ambiguous antiheroes, and thanks to everyone who wouldn't stop recommending this. <br /><br /><a href="thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10237067756321568996" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1917598190?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net" href="/user/show/7971097-bentley-bookbastion-net">Bentley ★ Bookbastion.net</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765335340" href="/book/show/13638125-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917598190" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11224007101750409875">A week or so ago I asked my feed for reading suggestions featuring strong villainous characters, and this book received nearly unanimous acclaim from the majority of my friends who saw the post and responded. Now, normally I kind of hesitate going into anything with high expectations, but I immediately ran out and bought it and now I just have to take a moment to tip my hat to to all my friends who suggested that I read it. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485963582ra/21865713.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><b>This book was EVERYTHING!</b> <br/><br/>I was so engaged by the story I was dreaded th</span>
  <span id="freeText11224007101750409875" style="display:none">A week or so ago I asked my feed for reading suggestions featuring strong villainous characters, and this book received nearly unanimous acclaim from the majority of my friends who saw the post and responded. Now, normally I kind of hesitate going into anything with high expectations, but I immediately ran out and bought it and now I just have to take a moment to tip my hat to to all my friends who suggested that I read it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485963582ra/21865713.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><b>This book was EVERYTHING!</b> <br><br>I was so engaged by the story I was dreaded the moments when I had to set the book down and go experience that awful thing called a social life. Really, who has time for the real world when there is a totally compelling story just waiting to be finished at home?!<br><br><b>Victor and Eli are absolute treasures.</b> They are so wonderfully written. Seriously. They're layered and diverse, while also being infuriatingly mad and deviously cunning at the same time. As far as anti-heros go: Victor was an absolute joy to experience the narrative journey through. Even when he's at his worst you can't help but root for him. Even Eli's decisions were so well crafted. I truly believed the way he rationalizes his behavior. This is characterization done right!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488247039i/22093526._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even the supporting cast of characters, Mitch, Syndney, Serena and Dominic are all wonderfully fleshed out. No one's backstory gets skimped out on in favor of pushing events in a certain direction. They're all given <i>compelling backstories</i> that inform on why they rationalize certain things they way they do. <b>We may not always agree with their decisions, but we're given reasons to understand them, which is so important.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488248344ra/22093611.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The pacing of this book is <i>so</i> engaging.</b> I was lost for the first 2 chapters, but once I got used to the narrative device Schwab employs, it got so compelling so quickly! I couldn't get through this book fast enough. I'm a busy dude right now thanks to numerous real life commitments, but I put my other current reads on hold for a few days just so I could carve my way though this book first. <br><br>I've read some great books already this year, but <b>this book just sort of blew them all out of the water.</b> I actually started this year off by reading my first book ever by Schwab, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10929432.The_Archived__The_Archived___1_" title="The Archived (The Archived, #1) by Victoria Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Archived</a> and I think it's safe to say that I'm becoming a HUGE fan. I'm definitely moving her Shades of Magic series up my tbr list soon! <br><br><b>5/5 stars &amp; a new favorite for me!</b><br><br><i>Buddy read with the wonderful</i> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/6278820-inge" rel="nofollow noopener">Inge</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3584738958995096232">on the scale of black to white, this book falls right down the middle. i have never read something so morally grey, so ethically ambiguous, so downright dark and absolutely pleasant at the same time. goodness me, this book was a trip in the best way possible. <br/><br/>i absolutely love the idea of anti-heroes. i love taking characters that we are meant to despise, but end up empathising and somewhat admiring them instead. maybe that makes me personally questionable, but wow. i loved how messed up and arr</span>
  <span id="freeText3584738958995096232" style="display:none">on the scale of black to white, this book falls right down the middle. i have never read something so morally grey, so ethically ambiguous, so downright dark and absolutely pleasant at the same time. goodness me, this book was a trip in the best way possible. <br /><br />i absolutely love the idea of anti-heroes. i love taking characters that we are meant to despise, but end up empathising and somewhat admiring them instead. maybe that makes me personally questionable, but wow. i loved how messed up and arrogant and broken both eli and victor were. their relationship was everything to me. from friends and confidants, to conspiratorial partners, to enemies. their relationship was just so demented and deranged, i couldnt look away. i love how the lines were blurred when it came to them. it was such a unique experience as a reader to see them at their worst and unravel the complex events which led them to that point. <br /><br />this book in its entirety is honestly something else. the concept, the plot, the characters, the writing, the conclusion. i couldnt put this down. and thank the book gods schwab decided to bless us with a sequel that our boys eli and victor so undoubtedly deserve. &lt;3<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

<div id="review_1121948998" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1121948998" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1121948998?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781785658679" href="/book/show/38087912-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1121948998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5880839267776878121"><b>Reread #2, Sept 2018</b><br/><br/>Apparently three years is enough to make me forget this book so entirely that it was practically like reading a new book. Which is a <i>smidge</i> disconcerting but OH WELL. <b>Needless to say! The reread was amazing.</b> And it was such moment of good memory feels because this was the first Schwab book I ever tried aww. I think <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_' title='A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Darker Shade of Magic</a> is perhaps my favourite of them all though. I actually was surprised how slow this one read. I don't remember it being slow?? But anyhow.<br/><br/>Al</span>
  <span id="freeText5880839267776878121" style="display:none"><b>Reread #2, Sept 2018</b><br><br>Apparently three years is enough to make me forget this book so entirely that it was practically like reading a new book. Which is a <i>smidge</i> disconcerting but OH WELL. <b>Needless to say! The reread was amazing.</b> And it was such moment of good memory feels because this was the first Schwab book I ever tried aww. I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22055262.A_Darker_Shade_of_Magic__Shades_of_Magic___1_" title="A Darker Shade of Magic (Shades of Magic, #1) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">A Darker Shade of Magic</a> is perhaps my favourite of them all though. I actually was surprised how slow this one read. I don't remember it being slow?? But anyhow.<br><br>Also Victor totally colours in books to chill out.<br><br>Also <b>this book is truly villainous and vicious</b> and specked with really heartwarming moments (a psychopath collecting smol strays and caring for them; a terrifying huge hacker drinking chocolate milk; an immortal looking superpowered man being pissed he's still being carded before buying a drink) and I think those are my favourite moments?!<br><br>I have full appreciation for how hard it must be to write a book with a timeline that bounces all over the place. MUCH RESPECT.<br><br>And I still fully envision this as Charles Xavier and Magneto, if their origin story had spun slightly differently. I'M SO READY FOR VENGEFUL. BRING IT.<br><br><br><br><u>
  <b>READ #1: May 2015</b>
</u><br><br><b>I THINK THIS BOOK WAS WRITTEN SPECIFICALLY FOR ME.</b> I love villains. I adore anti-heroes. I love a character with a complex backstory, a little bit of warped thinking, and a weakness for chocolate milk. THIS BOOK HAD IT ALL. I'm a billion percent pleased. <br><br><b>My main worry, before starting, is that I'm a 98% YA reader and this is an adult book.</b> But seriously? I didn't need to be worried. The writing is GOLDEN. It has less language/sex than a lot of YA books I read (!) and it's, in my opinion, just a teeny step away from YA anyway. Half the book the characters are in college, so only in their early twenties, and it's partially narrated by a 12yrs girl too. SO THERE. If you're worried about it being adult, dooon't be. <br><br><b>Can we talk about the villainousness?!!</b> I read sooo many books that claim to be about villains. BAH. Being a villain means you have a DARK side. Like really gritty and dark. Eli and Victor are two french fries short of a happy meal. They are <i>twisted</i>. They didnt' always start that way, though, which is what I love. Yeah they had issues...but this story encompasses them "Before They Turned Psycho" and then "After They Turned Psycho". But the ENTIRE cast is delicious and wonderful. Seriously everyone is fleshed out (except for one, but I'll explain) and it's soooo good to read. I ended up feeling badly for nearly everyone. <br><br><b>+ Victor:</b> He's probably the "main" protagonist of the story. Gah, how do I even describe him? He's very calm and confident and has a sharky smile and will risk everything and yet has a soft spot for lost people. He kind of picks up strays, which is entirely adorable. But at the same time, he'll kill a guy point blank and not even blink. SO YEAH THERE's THAT. <br><b>+ Eli: </b> Okay, he is just a screw loose. Even before their experiments started going crazy, Victor always described him as having a monster under his skin that sometimes peeked out. And Eli's also a religious nut. (Why are the religious ones always so crazy?!) So in the end, Eli wants to kill everyone with superpowers because he believes he's ordained by God to do so. Victor probably wouldn't have cared less, except that he and Eli are enemies and he's gotta be on the opposite side of Eli...just because. <br><b>+ Mitch: </b>I loved Mitch! He's like this huge hulk of a guy that works with Victor...and he looks like he'd smash your brain in his fist, but he's actually a tech genius. He also loves chocolate milke. <br><b>+ Sydney:</b> She's adorable! She's the 12 year old and her character development is insanely fantastic. <br><b>+ Serena:</b> She's Sydney's older sister. And while Sydney ends up with Victor, Serena ends up with Eli....and Serena is a bad nut. She controls people with her voice. Which is kind of a scary power...But when Eli wanted to kill Sydney and Serena went along with it? I HAD NO RESPECT FOR SERENA. <br><b>+Angie: </b> She's Eli's girlfriend in college and has no personality WHATSOEVER. It's really weird because everyone else is so incredible....<br><br><br><b>Basically it's like Charles Xavier and Magneto's origin story.</b> But mix that in with The Prestige movie, where there are two guys doing mostly bad things and how-do-you-root-for-either...but then one guy has a soft spot for kids, and the other guy isn't <i>meaning</i> to be so evil and -- UGH -- confusing emotions!!!<br><br><b>It's told in the present and past.</b> I didn't find this confusing at all, in fact, I loved it! One minute we'd be in the college, watching Eli and Victor spiral into their evil intentions. The next, we'd be in the future, with Sydney and Victor trying to stop the mad Eli from killing all the ExtraOrdinaries. Totally not confusing, perfectly marked, and the ends of the chapters are usually cliffhangers so I haaaaad to keep reading.<br><br><b>I also found it really addictive.</b> I usually am very aware of what page I'm on and how I'm tracking and blah blah, but this book?! TIME ESCAPED ME. And when I finished I felt like dashing to the library and getting every Schawb book I can find because -- WOW, JUST WOW.<b> It's incredible and perfect and totally my kind of story.</b> It's violent and vicious (duh) and writing by a master. The endign was PERFECT, although I didn't actually get any surprise moments in the book. It's marvellous, I think, but it's not particularly staggering for plot surprises. Which is fine by me, because I'm just in love with this book's existence. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430704402ra/14750315.gif" width="500" height="219" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>(This is basically Eli and Victor...except more evil.)</span>
  <a data-text-id="5880839267776878121" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
