    <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik"><img alt="Nilufer Ozmekik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559807601p2/53701594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2628541214?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=best-thriller">best-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2628541214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3537536404370741407">BAMMM!!! BAMMM!!BAMMM!! Nope this sound is not coming from my husband who repeatedly hits the axe to the kitchen door to save from cooking another disastrous, poisonous dish!<br/><br/>BAAAMMM!!! And again this sound doesn’t belong to my crazy neighbor who sings all day and parties at night, finally younger version of Robert Downey Jr. runs into his house with his car but sorry this is not also the voice of a car’s crushing into wall.<br/><br/>BAMM!! Yes, you got it right! I’m hitting my thick head against the wall </span>
  <span id="freeText3537536404370741407" style="display:none">BAMMM!!! BAMMM!!BAMMM!! Nope this sound is not coming from my husband who repeatedly hits the axe to the kitchen door to save from cooking another disastrous, poisonous dish!<br /><br />BAAAMMM!!! And again this sound doesn’t belong to my crazy neighbor who sings all day and parties at night, finally younger version of Robert Downey Jr. runs into his house with his car but sorry this is not also the voice of a car’s crushing into wall.<br /><br />BAMM!! Yes, you got it right! I’m hitting my thick head against the wall as a punishment not to read this series before. ( I firstly did it when I start “Bear and Nightingale” trilogy which turned into my all time favorite series. So yes, life is too short to procrastinate to read the best written books! Stop scrolling your phone or surfing through the channels air the shows for dumbs. Just read and read and read! I think this might be my quote or motto!)<br /><br />This is my upgraded review: And here we go: Victor and Eli’s competition to eliminate each other might be reminded you; Charles Xavier and Erik Lehsherr’s never ending rivalry ( personally I always had a hard time to choose between two hot man, with his sexy Scottish charisma McAvoy already stole my heart years ago but don’t forget Fassbender’s amazing Irish and German heritage, we saw the big parts of it at his movie “Shame”)<br /><br />So this book is a quite mash-up of X-Men – Boys ( because they are not originally super humans, they’re created at the labs as like Boys’ notorious super humans who are also bad guys like these two on this book!) –Flatliners ( if you skip Oliver Platt’s character, this reminds me of Bacon- Sutherland and Roberts trio. Two guys and a smart girl triangle)<br /><br />Story-telling is fast paced, stunning, entertaining. There are too many details seem like unimportant but you have to pay attention when you read some of Schwab’s books because every detail means something at the end to complete the entire puzzle and see the whole picture.<br /><br />All the characters have too many dark sides, complex, suffering from jealousy, hatred, narcissism and having sociopathic tendencies make most of the readers detest them and skip this book but I actually find this realistic and sensible because this book is not the heroes’ story who want to do the right thing. This is a battle between the pure evil and lighter evil: They both do whatever it takes to defeat the other.<br /><br />I also loved the sisters’ complex, deadly, love-hate relationship and cliffhanger at the end was the fantastic touch. So time to move on the next book! This author is evil master of dark thrilling, enjoyable books!</span>

I legitimately could not put it down. VE Schwab struck again! The complexity of the characters and the bouncing back and forth on the timeline and oh my goodness, if you're okay with reading about some college kids intentionally trying to kill themselves to get superpowers and maybe becoming accidental villains in the process PLEASE READ THIS (</span>

The complexity of the characters and the bouncing back and forth on the timeline and oh my goodness, if you're okay with reading about some college kids intentionally trying to kill themselves to get superpowers and maybe becoming accidental villains in the process PLEASE READ THIS (and if not that's totally okay too, it was just really good and thought provoking).</span>

<div id="review_1459618020" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1459618020" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1459618020?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765335340" href="/book/show/13638125-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1459618020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15625859245033341005"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538608549i/26397376._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Friends, this is my fifth book by VE Schwab, and I’ve three starred every single one of them. At this point, it is glaringly obvious that you should take my review(s) of her work with a grain of salt, because it is obviously a “me” thing. I will say that I adore the author, and I want so desperately to fall in love with a book of hers. And even though I thought <i>Vicious</i> would be the one, it sadly</span>
  <span id="freeText15625859245033341005" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1538608549i/26397376._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Friends, this is my fifth book by VE Schwab, and I’ve three starred every single one of them. At this point, it is glaringly obvious that you should take my review(s) of her work with a grain of salt, because it is obviously a “me” thing. I will say that I adore the author, and I want so desperately to fall in love with a book of hers. And even though I thought <i>Vicious</i> would be the one, it sadly wasn’t. <br><br>But this is a book about two college roommates who are literally experimenting with life and death and that tiny, minuscule, grey area in-between. Ten years later, a story of revenge, heartbreak, and anger is born. Yet, we still get glimpses into what happened at college ten years ago to bring these current ramifications into fruition. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I want to believe that there's more. That we could be more. Hell, we could be heroes.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book does raise the fascinating question, both in literature and in real life: what makes a hero and what makes a villain? Is it just the light the story is told in? Is the difference that monumental? Is it only a matter of perspective? Victor and Eli really challenge this question, and I adored it. <br> <br>➽ <b>Victor</b> - Fresh out of jail and will stop at nothing to exact his revenge; the slower the better.<br><br>➽ <b>Sydney</b> - My favorite character, who needs to be protected at all costs, and is just trying to find her place in a world that has constantly made her feel like she doesn’t belong. <br><br>➽ <b>Mitch</b> - I highkey loved this hacker and Victor’s soft friend. <br><br>➽ <b>Eli</b> - I actually hated Eli, and I think that’s the point of this book, truly, but his crisis of faith was just too much for me. <br><br>➽ <b>Serena</b> - To me, Serena and Sydney were truly the bright, shining stars of this story. And Serena has the coolest power of all the EOs, in my opinion.<br><br>And these five people’s paths all cross; some because of tangled pasts, but some because of brand new beginnings. And these characters quickly prove that developing superpowers could be pretty damn frightening. Especially when the powers you develop are rooted in who you are and what you need. <br><br>One thing I do want to briefly mention that I adored was Victor’s love for blackout poetry. I’ve actually never seen a book character have a passion for it, and it really warmed my heart. Every time he would create something, it really would take my breath away. It was such a bright light in the story for me. <br><br>I read this with a few friends, and the reading was broken down over the course of five days. Day one and day five were both, easily, five star reading days. I loved the start and end of this book more than words. Again, Victoria Schwab is so intelligent, and her ideas are truly a tier above the rest. Sadly, the middle three days I just felt a bit bored, and it only got worse by day four. But the ending? God, I know I shouldn’t, but I desperately want to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2421162496" rel="nofollow noopener">Vengeful</a> now. <br><br>I also really truly loved how the first and last chapter began. I’m always a sucker when authors mirror events and phrases throughout their book(s) and I feel like VE Schwab always successfully does this. And I get goosebumps each and every time. <br><br>Overall, I get that there is some kind of disconnect between me and this author’s books. And nothing is changing that because, believe me, I truly want to love her work so badly. Like I said above, take this review with a grain of salt because so many of my friends adore this book, and I really implore you to check out some of their amazing reviews: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1977347311?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Em</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/730495760?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Adriana</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1250020679?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">CW</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2035933180?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Hari</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223813611?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Mari</a>!<br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><b>Content and trigger warnings</b> for talk of suicide, attempted suicide, overdosing, self-harm, drug use, murder, animal death, abandonment, and depiction of panic attacks.<br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/10113250-mo" rel="nofollow noopener">Mo</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7345713-paloma" rel="nofollow noopener">Paloma</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14843185.Julie_Zantopoulos" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4807883.Amber_LaShell" rel="nofollow noopener">Amber</a>! ❤</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1256391395" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12201636239074769246"><i>“There are no good men in this game.”</i><br/><br/>I'm in a Victoria Schwab fever. Can't really blame her though, her novels are amazing!<br/><br/>The most interesting thing about <i> Vicious </i> were its characters with their extraordinary abilities and the fact that there is no "good" main character. Both, protagonist and antagonist do ruthless things and leave a trail of violence and death, one more than the other. But I ended up rooting for some of the side characters and - of course - the dog.<br/>Eli however really disguste</span>
  <span id="freeText12201636239074769246" style="display:none"><i>“There are no good men in this game.”</i><br /><br />I'm in a Victoria Schwab fever. Can't really blame her though, her novels are amazing!<br /><br />The most interesting thing about <i> Vicious </i> were its characters with their extraordinary abilities and the fact that there is no "good" main character. Both, protagonist and antagonist do ruthless things and leave a trail of violence and death, one more than the other. But I ended up rooting for some of the side characters and - of course - the dog.<br />Eli however really disgusted me. He was ignorant, self-righteous and fanatic. I hate people like him, they make me angry and mad. They remind me of Dolores Umbridge and there is no one in the world of fiction I hate more than her.<br />It also helps that Victoria Schwab is an incredible writer. A master of atmosphere and originality. Someone who creates characters so intiguing and compelling that it's impossible to lose interest in them. Just add some superpowers and you have the perfect story.<br />I'm in love.<br /><br /><i>13/03/2016</i><br /><br />Aaand we're getting a sequel! Whoop whoop! I'm really happy, since there was so much room left for a follow-up. Can't wait for <i>Vengeful</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2059723148?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765335340" href="/book/show/13638125-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=adult-fantasy-sci-fi">adult-fantasy-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=crime-mystery-thriller">crime-mystery-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2059723148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10287059140156008867"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511224764ra/24493716.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Reading about messed up lunatics had never felt better, full satisfaction guaranteed.<br/><br/>A twisted tale of friendships, bitter jealousy, betrayal, loss and ultimately of revenge, Vicious is about Victor and Eli, former friends turned foes who also happen to be deviously cunning in (almost) equal measures. <br/><br/>Neither one can be categorised as simply good or evil and unlike many stories of similar kinds, this is in no way a tale of good vs. evil as there are no good guys in this scenario. <br/>They’re both bo</span>
  <span id="freeText10287059140156008867" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511224764ra/24493716.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Reading about messed up lunatics had never felt better, full satisfaction guaranteed.<br><br>A twisted tale of friendships, bitter jealousy, betrayal, loss and ultimately of revenge, Vicious is about Victor and Eli, former friends turned foes who also happen to be deviously cunning in (almost) equal measures. <br><br>Neither one can be categorised as simply good or evil and unlike many stories of similar kinds, this is in no way a tale of good vs. evil as there are no good guys in this scenario. <br>They’re both borderline psychopaths and narcissistic as shit. Tell me you're not in love already...<br><br>As far as anti-heroes go, Victor is an absolute delight. Even when most of his actions leave you astounded and amazed, you can’t help but love and fear him all at once, whilst rooting for him to come out on top. He really messes with your sense of logic. It’s a ‘lesser of two evils’ kind of a thing.<br><br>Eli is a whole other story. Though he is brilliant with frighteningly well-crafted plans, he’s incredibly ignorant, fanatic and his lack of empathy and self-righteousness make Victor seem like an angelic hero. He seriously takes the cake on the whole MESSED UP front. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511920128ra/24556456.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What more could you ask for in your characters than when they’re so delightfully grey and blur the lines between good and evil? <br><br>Each of the supporting characters is also intricately narrated and as their compelling backstories are slowly revealed, we’re made to understand their actions and decisions. Seriously, everybody’s messed up and it couldn’t be more delightful. <br><br>The entire concept and deliberation is just brilliant. <br><br>Go, Schwab! ✊ Just go read it... simple as that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10287059140156008867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2282402472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2282402472" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2282402472?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250160263" href="/book/show/36342017-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=best-of-2013">best-of-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2282402472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6564360508493199217"><i>BRILLIANT. ABSOLUTELY BRILLIANT. I BLOODY LOVED THIS.</i><br/><br/><b>“Humans, monsters, heroes, villains—to Victor it was all just a matter of semantics. Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. Someone else could be labelled a villain for trying to stop them. Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.”</b><br/><br/>I thought this would be a lot more <b>X-Men</b>-ish with tonnes of fight scenes and action sequences, but this was more of a <b>psychological </b></span>
  <span id="freeText6564360508493199217" style="display:none"><i>BRILLIANT. ABSOLUTELY BRILLIANT. I BLOODY LOVED THIS.</i><br><br><b>“Humans, monsters, heroes, villains—to Victor it was all just a matter of semantics. Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. Someone else could be labelled a villain for trying to stop them. Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.”</b><br><br>I thought this would be a lot more <b>X-Men</b>-ish with tonnes of fight scenes and action sequences, but this was more of a <b>psychological debate</b> over <i>good vs evil</i>. Rather than <b>supervillains</b>, we were following the paths of <b>sociopathic serial killers</b>, which was fascinating, albeit unexpected. I began the novel preferring <b>Eli</b>, and ended it rooting for <b>Victor</b>. I still can’t say which is the <b>hero</b> and which is the <b>villain</b>, considering that neither of them have any qualms about killing other people. They’re both equally <i>evil</i> <b>psychopaths</b>. <br><br><i>“Hate was too simple a word. He and Eli were bonded, by blood and death and science. They were alike, more so now than ever. And he had missed Eli. He wanted to see him. And he wanted to see him suffer. He wanted to see the look in Eli’s eyes when he lit them up with pain. He wanted his attention. Eli was like a thorn beneath Victor’s skin, and it hurt. He could turn off every nerve in his body, but Victor couldn’t do a damned thing about the twinge he felt when he thought of Cardale.”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549234330i/27011097._SX540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Victor Vale</b> was definitely my <i>favourite</i> character. He was, by no means a good person, considering that he convinced his roommate, Eli, that conducting an <b>experiment</b> which requires them to <i>scientifically die</i> in order to be reborn as <b>EO</b>’s (Extra Ordinaries) was a <b>good idea</b>, and the fact that he got the aforementioned roommate’s girlfriend, Angie, <i>killed</i> as a result of the experiment. <i>BUT</i>, I still loved him??? I don’t know what that says about me, haha. <br><br><i>“You don’t think I’m a bad person. I don’t want to prove you wrong.”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549234330i/27011098._SX540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While, Victor was pretty much the <b>King of Bad Decisions</b>, whether it be <b>murder or torture</b>, he was also <i>caring</i> when he wanted to be. Although he initially had ulterior motives when he invited <b>Sydney and Mitch</b> into the fold, he did come to genuinely be fond of them and the little group that they had formed. <b>Dol</b> was also an adorable addition to this newfound criminal family. <br><br><i>“The paper called Eli a hero. The word made Victor laugh. Not just because it was absurd, but because it posed a question. If Eli really was a hero, and Victor meant to stop him, did that make him a villain?”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549234330i/27011099._SX540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Eliot Cardale</b>, later known as Eli Ever, on the other hand, I wasn’t as fond of. I didn’t like his <i>holier than thou</i> attitude, thinking that he was <b>chosen by God</b> to essentially play God, by acting as <b>judge, jury, and executioner</b>, where he decided who was worthy to live or die. What makes him so special that he thinks it’s his <i>duty to exterminate</i> everyone with abilities? Having supernatural abilities shouldn’t be a crime, as what matters is what you <i>DO</i> with the abilities. The ability itself isn’t bad. If you have the power of <i>hydrokinesis</i>, the power could be used for <b>good</b> if you’re creating water for someone who’s thirsty, or the power could be used for <b>evil</b> if you’re creating water to fill someone’s lungs and kill them. It depends on <i>HOW</i> it’s used. Also, it’s so hypocritical of Eli, considering that he has abilities, as well. It’s such a <b>Hitler</b>-esque thing to do. Hitler only wanted Aryan Germans, despite not being Aryan himself. <br><br>In addition, Eli refused to <i>LISTEN</i> to Victor, assuming the worst of his friend, which was the <i>catalyst</i> for everything to come in the novel. Everything that occurred could have been <b>averted</b>, if Eli had <b>stopped to listen</b>. Instead, he was responsible for betraying Victor, which set Victor on the path for revenge against Eli. <br><br>This was such an <b>engaging novel</b> that I nearly <b>devoured</b> in one sitting (Why does uni exist? Honestly, why?!). I was glued to the edge of my seat, as I was <i>SO INVESTED</i> in these characters and <i>SO DESPERATE</i> to see how everything would unfold. I didn’t think that I’d like this as much as I ended up liking it. The <i>Shades of Magic</i> trilogy is still my favourite work of Schwab’s, but this is more of what I wanted from the <i>Monsters of Verity</i> duology. <i>THIS</i> was the <b>dark and gritty</b> story that I desired. It was so <b>twisted</b>, being centred on <b>ambition for power</b>, <b>betrayal among friends</b>, and <b>hunger for revenge</b>. And <i>I LOVED IT</i>. I can’t wait to see them all again in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26856502.Vengeful__Villains___2_" title="Vengeful (Villains, #2) by V.E. Schwab" rel="nofollow noopener">Vengeful</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6564360508493199217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2560003623" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2560003623" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2560003623?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/18483489-vicious">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/1695365-victoria-schwab">Victoria Schwab</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2560003623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1956440956680966161"><i>"If no one else agrees with you, chances are you're wrong."</i><br/><br/><b>If it's wrong to be in love with Victor Vale then I don't want to be right. </b><br/><br/>Seriously guys, how did you all read this years ago and wait patiently for <i>Vengeful</i> to be published? In all honesty, I never put this one off because of the delayed sequel; in fact, I put it off for so long because hyped books + me typically don't end well. This is one of the VERY few cases where the hype actually is understated. It is precisely the type of book </span>
  <span id="freeText1956440956680966161" style="display:none"><i>"If no one else agrees with you, chances are you're wrong."</i><br /><br /><b>If it's wrong to be in love with Victor Vale then I don't want to be right. </b><br /><br />Seriously guys, how did you all read this years ago and wait patiently for <i>Vengeful</i> to be published? In all honesty, I never put this one off because of the delayed sequel; in fact, I put it off for so long because hyped books + me typically don't end well. This is one of the VERY few cases where the hype actually is understated. It is precisely the type of book I want to shove into everyone's hands and scream "READ THIS!", because how could you not love it? <s>Obviously I understand that not every book is for everyone so please don't @ me.</s><br /><br />I don't want to ramble on, because I'm just about the last person to read this book for the first time, but I definitely could fangirl for eternity over this one. Folks, <i>Vicious</i> had everything I could want and need plus more. The characters were outstanding, the premise and plot execution were exquisite, and that final chapter was incredibly satisfying. I can totally see why Queen Schwab expanded Eli and Victor's feud into a sequel; these villains were simply to complex and substantial to confine to a single installment. <br /><br />If you haven't read the book yet, or are looking to do a reread because you haven't gotten to part two, I highly recommend giving the audio version a go. I had a blast listening to the audible version; the narrator had a clean and clear reading voice and did various characters with a talented distinction-no cheeseball accents here! Highly recommended and feel this is in my top 3 audible reads (listens?) of the year!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1956440956680966161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_737465818" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/737465818" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/737465818?book_show_action=true">Oct 08, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765335340" href="/book/show/13638125-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=on-the-run">on-the-run</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alternate-universe">alternate-universe</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=religious-spiritual">religious-spiritual</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer737465818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17148464653808057682"><b>Actual rating: 3.5</b><br/><br/>This is a book about superheroes---or rather, antiheroes, that started off wonderfully, but gradually wandered into genericville territory. It was still very good, but I'm still left with a sense of disappointment. The characters in this book didn't live up to my expectations, or to their own potential. It was the equivalent of a movie-based comic book adaptation, and granted, there have been pretty amazing ones...but still, this is a book. <b>A book has so much more potential for</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17148464653808057682" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 3.5</b><br /><br />This is a book about superheroes---or rather, antiheroes, that started off wonderfully, but gradually wandered into genericville territory. It was still very good, but I'm still left with a sense of disappointment. The characters in this book didn't live up to my expectations, or to their own potential. It was the equivalent of a movie-based comic book adaptation, and granted, there have been pretty amazing ones...but still, this is a book. <b>A book has so much more potential for plot twists, for character development, and ultimately, this book didn't live up to my high expectations of it.</b> The quality of the writing is excellent, the character portrayals very well done, but the narrative style didn't work for me, and I had a lot of issues with how cookie-cutter some things eventually became. <br /><br />If you had asked me how many stars I would give this book, based on the first 5 or so chapters, I would have said five, no questions about it. The beginning was amazing, the first chapter had hook that pulled me in right from the start. We have people digging up a corpse in the middle of a frigid night. We have a talking, walking girl who just might be dead.<br /><br />This is the present, and we are rapidly brought back to the past...to Lockland University, 10 years ago, where two young men named Victor Vale and Eli Cardale were best friends. Lockland University is the destination of the best and the brightest, and Victor and Eli are the elite among the elites. They share the same intensity for learning, the same sharp brilliance, and a quiet, unspoken rivalry when it comes to life, education, and love. They are like-minded with their fierce ambition, but of the two, Eli seems to be the more sinister, despite his charming, carefree façade.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>...something about Eli was decidedly wrong. He was like one of those pictures full of small errors, the kind you could only pick out by searching the image from every angle, and even then, a few always slipped by. On the surface, Eli seemed perfectly normal, but now and then Victor would catch a crack, a sideways glance, a moment when his roommate’s face and his words, his look and his meaning, would not line up. Those fleeting slices fascinated Victor. It was like watching two people, one hiding in the other’s skin. And their skin was always too dry, on the verge of cracking and showing the color of the thing beneath.</i>
</blockquote>For their Comprehensive Science Seminar thesis, Eli unexpectedly chooses the topics of EO: ExtraOrdinary people. People with special abilities, specifically, how science...biology, chemistry, psychology...could explain their existence.<br /><br />An ambitious topic, a creative topic...one that instills a bitter jealousy within Victor. He feels compelled to push Eli further, as they think of ways in which they can trigger these special abilities and become EOs themselves. Victor and Eli become the guinea pigs in their own science experiments, and their hubris goes too far. It works, albeit disastrously.<br /><br />10 years later, Victor has broken out of prison. Accompanying him is <i>"a hacker, a half-dead dog, and a child"</i>. And he is out for revenge. He slowly tracks Eli down and draws him out, thanks to the help from his ragtag crew, the aforementioned child and a hulking gentle giant of a hacker. Like all superhero movies, everything leads up to a final, grand confrontation.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>Victor was out. Victor was free.<br />And Victor was coming for Eli—just as he’d promised he would.<br />He sunk the shovel into the cold earth with a satisfying thud.</i>
</blockquote><b>It took me awhile to realize that this book took place in a pseudo-alternative universe</b>. It's still the current world, as we know it, but it's more like a comic book world, because these EOs are not just theoretical. They're not exactly famous, but it is known that these people exist. It confused me a bit until I realized this fact, because this world seems so similar to our own that it is a little bit of a shock to the system to hear people---specifically, science professors, who are accepting and actually receptive to the idea of a thesis involving people with special powers.<br /><br />What I loved about this book was the writing and the character portrayals. There are no clear cut, no clear message of goodness versus evil here. Both characters can be termed "bad," respectively, even our main narrator, whom we are presumably expected to root for. Victor is not a good man, he has some redeemable qualities, but throughout the novels, his good deeds are tempered with sparks of inhumanity, of violence. He shoots a man, he inflicts pain, he tortures people when it suits his purposes.<br /><br />I had a problem with Eli's character development. He is a good "villain," if you can call him that, but <b>I felt like his development was out of character and inconsistent from what we know of him.</b> It felt like a bit of a cop-out, an easy way to pin the donkey's tail on a character designed to be bad, if you will. Eli's evolution was unbelievable, nonsensical. <b>He turned from a brilliant boy, a normal boy with a crack beneath surface into a madman overnight.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“What gives you the right to play judge and jury and executioner?”<br />“God.”</i>
</blockquote>Eli has always been somewhat religious, it's a contradictory fact about him that Victor finds fascinating, but it is as if he becomes a hypocritical fundamentalist Christian in his rock-solid belief of fulfilling his God-given duty out of nowhere. He did suffer through some traumatic events in the beginning of the novel, but I felt that it was insufficient in explaining his personality changes. It's not enough. <b>It turns Eli from a villain with a potentially complex inner darkness into just another fanatically religious, self-righteous trope.</b><br /><br />I had a problem with the constant flashbacks in the narrative. It fluctuates a lot. It goes from the present to 10 years past, to last night, to 2 hours ago, to 2 days ago. The chapters are labeled, so that you know where that particular chapter is taken place, during what time, but honestly, it got to be a little too much. The narrative is from a third-person perspective, and we get it from many characters, Victor, Eli, Sydney, Serena, Mitch. It wasn't so bad, because most of the narrative focused around Sydney, Eli, and Victor, but it didn't mesh together well when combined with all the constant flashbacks.<br /><br /><b>Overall, I still would highly recommend this</b>. The writing is spectacular, and the characters are mostly well-done, with the exception of Eli. My complaints with this book are subjective, and I still enjoyed the book despite what I felt to be its faults.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17148464653808057682" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2315206661" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315206661" />
    <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk"><img alt="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597641717p2/66224803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315206661?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk" href="/user/show/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk">Jessi ♥️ H. Vojsk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781250160263" href="/book/show/36342017-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66224803-jessi-h-vojsk?shelf=my-absolute-favorite">my-absolute-favorite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315206661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15294042746442612560"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522346786ra/25292414.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> “But these words people threw around - humans, monsters, heroes, villains - to Victor it was all just a matter of semantics. <br/>Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. <br/>Someone else could be labeled a villain for trying to stop them. <br/>Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>There’s always the story involving a hero and a villain. Someone who’s good and someone who’s bad. <br/>But who decides on which sid</span>
  <span id="freeText15294042746442612560" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1522346786ra/25292414.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> “But these words people threw around - humans, monsters, heroes, villains - to Victor it was all just a matter of semantics. <br>Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. <br>Someone else could be labeled a villain for trying to stop them. <br>Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.” </i> <br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>There’s always the story involving a hero and a villain. Someone who’s good and someone who’s bad. <br>But who decides on which side you are? Who tells you that you’re the good guy or the evil one? <br>Well, sometimes it’s your mind telling you that the things you do are right. More or less. <br>That’s why Eli Ever is killing EOs - extraordinary people with powers - one by one. <br>And Victor - his former best friend and prisoner for at least ten years - is hunting him down for locking him up. <br>This book is definitely one of a kind. It’s really slow - like nearly all of Victoria Schwabs books - but the story/characters/world/writing is phenomenal (like always). <br>There isn’t much happening through the beginning, but we get to know how Eli and Victor met, what happened and we get to see what Victors evil plan is. <br>I really really liked this book. It was definitely entertaining, even though it had a really slow pacing. I especially liked that the ending and the beginning ended nearly the same. <br>All in all it’s a real masterpiece and I can’t wait for the second book! <br><br>Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Victor Vale is now officially one of my favorite villains/characters. We don’t get to know much about his past (at least what happened before he went to college), but we get to know that he’s extremely intelligent and interesting. <br>My favorite parts were the ones where Victor acted like a real life dad. <br>Caring for his kids (Mitch, Dol and Sydney) and always looking out for them, even though he sometimes does it too strictly. <br>Then there is Eli. I was really fascinated by him. The way he explains and justifies his murders/actions is kind of fanatic. The way he thinks god is approving everything he does, makes him such an interesting character. He’s always in doubt and tries to finish his “duty”, but is always torn between his own believes and the things he sees and feels. <br>The “side” characters in this story - Sydney, Mitch and Serena are also brilliantly created. They’re kind of twisted and all of them have their own personality and background story. <br>All in all Victoria Schwab did a great job creating the characters. They catch your interest immediately and they do feel very real. <br><br>World ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Superheroes, villains and sidekicks. There are many worlds involving them. DC, Marvel, we all heard of them, maybe even watched the movies or read the comics. <br>But in some way they never felt like the real world. But with Victoria’s story “Vicious” it does. <br>It feels like it could happen anytime. <br>Soon there will be other people - extraordinary people that don’t fit into the „normal“ world. <br>People that survived a near death experience, but survived. <br>They’re all survivors. <br>But surviving something means that you sometimes loose something in the process. <br>You gain and you loose. <br>But you never remain the same. <br><br>Relationships ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Oh man oh man. Victoria Schwab was never the author for a fluffy, erotic or passionate love story. <br>In her stories she focuses more on friendships, families. People you choose to live with. <br>And in this book we focus on Eli’s and Victors past friendship and the new „family“ Victor found himself. I loved them all and if I was a character living in this book I would definitely be in Team Victor. <br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>Victoria is a mastermind in writing, no doubt in that. But the way she slows her pacing is sometimes a little bit dragging. It was a brilliant book that jumps through the time - from past to present - and has different POVs, that make the story so much more intriguing and interesting.<br><br>First reread ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>I still love this book so much. Absolute favorite ♥️</span>
  <a data-text-id="15294042746442612560" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1455035502" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455035502" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455035502?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765335340" href="/book/show/13638125-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455035502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2222540638778442176"><i>
  <b>“Be lost. Give up. Give In. in the end It would be better to surrender before you begin. be lost. Be lost And then you will not care if you are ever found.”</b>
</i><br/><br/>I've  heard all over Goodreads about how amazing VE Schwab is. How everything she writes is amazing. With the hype came me putting off reading this book. So, when <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7027484-sandra' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sandra</a>  picked this book out for us to buddy read I was happy that I would finally get around to it. <br/><br/><i>Vicious</i> follows Victor and Eli who were best friends and college roommates. </span>
  <span id="freeText2222540638778442176" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Be lost. Give up. Give In. in the end It would be better to surrender before you begin. be lost. Be lost And then you will not care if you are ever found.”</b>
</i><br><br>I've  heard all over Goodreads about how amazing VE Schwab is. How everything she writes is amazing. With the hype came me putting off reading this book. So, when <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7027484-sandra" rel="nofollow noopener">Sandra</a>  picked this book out for us to buddy read I was happy that I would finally get around to it. <br><br><i>Vicious</i> follows Victor and Eli who were best friends and college roommates. When it comes time for their college thesis assignment starts the two of them begin working on the idea that under the right circumstances you could give a person extraordinary abilities. The two decide to take their theories a step further, and goes from idea to an experiment gone wrong. Ten years later Victor breaks out of prison determined to find Eli again, but when they meet again they will be meeting as enemies. <br><br>Victor and Eli are some of my all time favorite male characters. Getting characters that are as dark, morally grey, and layered as these two is hard to find. They are complete anti-heroes. It's amazing how they can both be the hero and villain of the story, and that Schwab easily wrote them so. Victor and Eli character wise have the same relationship as Professor X and Magneto in Xmen. Eli is this smooth talking, genius, with the killer smile. While Victor is more of the odd ball loner. Them being two polar opposites perfectly sets them up to be enemies. Each of them brings so much to the table. Victor and Eli felt very real. That's because each of  them had their own opinions about right and wrong. They both had this odd way of hating each other while admiring each other. This making them not only some of my favorite characters, but help build how complex and unique they both were. when it came to side characters, they were also flawless. There's one character I wont talk about. I know it wont be a spoiler if I did, but I honestly rather leave them out just in case. However the other two are Sydney and Mitch. Mitch is one of those characters you know you'll like right away, but still know he'll take some warming up to. His character is slowly revealed and as his traits are given to us, you'll fall in love with him. Plus all this quirky aspects didn't hurt. Sydney was my favorite character in the book. I loved how she was both an innocent and kind of evil at the same time. She's cute, funny, and her back story is amazing. <br><br>When it came to the plot-line for <i>Vicious </i>I just couldn't get enough of it. The opening scene of this book will without a doubt pull you in. It's one of the best opening scenes I've read, and perfectly sets the dark tone of the novel. From then on the novel bounces back and forth between past, present, and then even hourly. The first part of the novel breaks down how the two meet how their experiment became, and how to two turned enemies. I loved how deep and dark Schwab took the start of this story. Every little detail is perfectly planted. I couldn't get over why a certain person got the powers they did. It's perfection. The last half of the book is where all the set up, and add ons start revealing themselves. All this leading up to the epic conclusion of an ending.  You know eventually the two will come face to face and when it happens you wont be let-down, because in the end... <br><br><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-qvYjJ4dQSp4/V7HSYEPgvEI/AAAAAAAAD2w/r21BSjdSHYwF1q5FIBDFO9xvK7E0KKMswCLcB/s1600/vicious.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="134" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471272321ra/20018707.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>Vicious</i> was the perfect summer buddy read. I died when I heard there will be a second book, because that ending. Also re-died when I heard this has been opted for a movie. The entire time I was reading this I could see it playing out so perfectly on film.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2222540638778442176" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1717020888" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1717020888?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Luna. ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Luna. ✨" href="/user/show/53385361-lady-luna">Lady Luna. ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780765335340" href="/book/show/13638125-vicious">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53385361-lady-luna?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1717020888" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10998441280779437878"><b>4/5</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “But these words people threw around - humans, monsters, heroes, villains - to Victor it was all just a matter of semantics. Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. Someone else could be labeled a villain for trying to stop them. Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/>Okay so I have always wanted to read vicious, I swear I've had it on my tbr since I was born. Why? Well because that blurb sounde</span>
  <span id="freeText10998441280779437878" style="display:none"><b>4/5</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote> “But these words people threw around - humans, monsters, heroes, villains - to Victor it was all just a matter of semantics. Someone could call themselves a hero and still walk around killing dozens. Someone else could be labeled a villain for trying to stop them. Plenty of humans were monstrous, and plenty of monsters knew how to play at being human.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Okay so I have always wanted to read vicious, I swear I've had it on my tbr since I was born. Why? Well because that blurb sounded oh so delicious, I love anti heros ! As soon as I received Vicious I was so excited to devour it, just like I would a cheesecake. Upon the first page of the novel, I stumbled across this quote; <b>
  <i>"Life—the way it really is—is a battle not between Bad and Good, but between Bad and Worse.<br>—Joseph Brodsky”</i>
</b><br><i>THIS IS MY NEW FAVOURITE QUOTE. </i>Its the most truthful thing I've ever read in my life.<b> It was love at page one, </b>and my love for this novel only seemed to increase, <u>until that ending. I WANTED MORE BADASSERY! </u>I went through the whole book enjoying it but that ending was so flat. I feel like the ending could have been way better. But that's really my only complaint and that's just my opinion. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>"The absence of pain led to an absence of fear, and the absence of fear led to a disregard for consequences.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Okay so enough bad stuff. I don't think I can flail and yell enough about this book, I wish I could write this whole review in caps to get my point across however that's hard work on an iPhone and I'm extremely lazy. This book was the bomb, I'm so inlove with it. Everything is just so amazing, I loved the plot so much, it was exciting, fun &amp; full of WOW moments, theres only one word to describe it and that's COOL. It's basically about two best friends who start experimenting with near death experiences. Some stuff happens then bam Victor is in jail and escapes with one thing on his mind to kill ELI (his old bestfriend). The book is multiple POV but with Victor as the main and most common POV. The storyline is dark and it is set in a really strange way, it's in past tense ten years ago, current day &amp; days after Victors escape, so it's kinda jumpy however she nailed it and it totally worked, <b>so I'm going to applaud Schwab for pulling it off. </b>The characters were so goddamn amazing, we have our protagonist Victor Vale who I adored with every inch of my black heart. Seriously he had my heart captured as soon as he escaped jail *swoons*, I LOVE BADASS MC's. And he was so bad, like villainous and malicious bad. So PRECIOUS &amp; quite evil. I totally get why people find him hard to like, <b>I however was made for Victor Vale. </b> My favourite Victor Vale quote; <b>
  <i>“Because you don't think I'm a bad person," he said. "And I don't want to prove you wrong.” </i>
</b><br>I also love Sydney and Mitch, both were incredibly entertaining background characters. Our antagonist is a sadistic bastard who is like a crazed religious person<b> (I mean NO offence to any religion or extremely religious people or any crazy people in fact! Don't take my words as an attack. The antagonist is actually a psycho, and if you read the book, you'll understand what I mean). </b>I always know books are gonna end up hectic when our antagonist is doing things for the 'greater good'. There was lots of death and good shit. And quite possibly the best anti superhero book I've ever read. It's the only one I've read, so it's not up against anything however it was the greatest &amp; you should just read the goddamn book. Also if you haven't yet noticed, it was extremely quotable.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491386947i/22404585._SX540_.jpg" width="700" height="850" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I love Schwabs writing style, its very simple and I like simple. She is a fantastic writer and I'm definitely looking forward to some more adult stuff from her <b>and I'll be dying until book two is released. Like bury me now and revive me once it arrives, I can't take the waiting already.</b><br><br><b>Ps I heard this is gonna be a movie ?!</b> <br>*extreme arm and leg flailling*<br><br><b>
  <i>I wouldn't recommend this book to the YA community due to the amount of drug use in it. So definitely recommended to all mature beings (15+).</i>
</b><br><br><i> You can find this review &amp; some others on my <a href="https://lunathemoonchild.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Wordpress </a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10998441280779437878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_40642172'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40642172-this-savage-song"><img alt="This Savage Song (Monsters of Verity, #1)" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1529942103l/40642172._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SFADAwExAU7a0OQI48gfpo7Knd0kIdOqY6E6tss+GHUZ4ohRqiWHOO0l4ZS9afKHZEU5QD8ipbocnog136kSlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
